**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Rename SchedulerProfile to SchedulingProfile

## Objective
Rename `SchedulerProfile` to `SchedulingProfile` in the Kubernetes scheduler
to follow the API naming convention (action-noun pattern).

## Requirements

1. **Rename the type** (likely in scheduler config or profile package):
   - `type SchedulerProfile struct` → `type SchedulingProfile struct`

2. **Update all references** (15+ call sites):
   - `pkg/scheduler/` — scheduler internals
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/kube-scheduler/` — API types
   - Config and profile loading code
   - Test files

3. **Update constructor functions** and factory methods

## Key Reference Files
- `pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go` — profile definition
- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` — uses profiles
- `staging/src/k8s.io/kube-scheduler/config/` — API config types

## Success Criteria
- `SchedulerProfile` no longer used as type name
- `SchedulingProfile` used instead
- 80%+ of references updated

Disabled plugins are any of the default plugins that\\\\n120: \\\\t// should be disabled.\\\\n121: \\\\t// When no enabled or disabled plugin is specified for an extension point,\\\\n122: \\\\t// default plugins for that extension point will be used if there is any.\\\\n123: \\\\t// If a QueueSort plugin is specified, the same QueueSort Plugin and\\\\n124: \\\\t// PluginConfig must be specified for all profiles.\\\\n125: \\\\tPlugins *Plugins\\\\n126: \\\\n127: \\\\t// PluginConfig is an optional set of custom plugin arguments for each plugin.\\\\n128: \\\\t// Omitting config args for a plugin is equivalent to using the default config\\\\n129: \\\\t// for that plugin.\\\\n130: \\\\tPluginConfig []PluginConfig\\\\n131: }\\\\n132: \\\\n133: // Plugins include multiple extension points. When specified, the list of plugins for\\\\n134: // a particular extension point are the only ones enabled. If an extension point is\\\\n135: // omitted from the config, then the default set of plugins is used for that extension point.\\\\n136: // Enabled plugins are called in the order specified here, after default plugins. If they need to\\\\n137: // be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\\\\n138: type Plugins struct {\\\\n139: \\\\t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\\\\n140: \\\\tPreEnqueue PluginSet\\\\n141: \\\\n142: \\\\t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\\\\n143: \\\\tQueueSort PluginSet\\\\n144: \\\\n145: \\\\t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \\\\\\\"PreFilter\\\\\\\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\\\\n146: \\\\tPreFilter PluginSet\\\\n147: \\\\n148: \\\\t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\\\\n149: \\\\tFilter PluginSet\\\\n150: \\\\n151: \\\\t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\\\\n152: \\\\tPostFilter PluginSet\\\\n153: \\\\n154: \\\\t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\\\\n155: \\\\tPreScore PluginSet\\\\n156: \\\\n157: \\\\t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\\\\n158: \\\\tScore PluginSet\\\\n159: \\\\n160: \\\\t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\\\\n161: \\\\t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\\\\n162: \\\\tReserve PluginSet\\\\n163: \\\\n164: \\\\t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\\\\n165: \\\\tPermit PluginSet\\\\n166: \\\\n167: \\\\t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\\\\n168: \\\\tPreBind PluginSet\\\\n169: \\\\n170: \\\\t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \\\\\\\"Bind\\\\\\\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\\\\n171: \\\\t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\\\\n172: \\\\tBind PluginSet\\\\n173: \\\\n174: \\\\t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\\\\n175: \\\\tPostBind PluginSet\\\\n176: \\\\n177: \\\\t// MultiPoint is a simplified config field for enabling plugins for all valid extension points\\\\n178: \\\\tMultiPoint PluginSet\\\\n179: }\\\\n180: \\\\n181: // PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\\\\n182: // If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\\\\n183: type PluginSet struct {\\\\n184: \\\\t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\\\\n185: \\\\t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\\\\n186: \\\\tEnabled []Plugin\\\\n187: \\\\t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\\\\n188: \\\\t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \\\\\\\"*\\\\\\\" should be provided.\\\\n189: \\\\tDisabled []Plugin\\\\n190: }\\\\n191: \\\\n192: // Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. \\t\\t\\t}\\n132: \\t\\t}\\n133: \\t}\\n134: \\treturn nil\\n135: }\\n136: \\n137: // KubeSchedulerProfile is a scheduling profile.\\n138: type KubeSchedulerProfile struct {\\n139: \\t// SchedulerName profile.\\n142: \\tSchedulerName *string `json:\\\"schedulerName,omitempty\\\"`\\n143: \\n144: \\t// PercentageOfNodesToScore is the percentage of all nodes that once found feasible\\n145: \\t// for running a pod, the scheduler stops its search for more feasible nodes in\\n146: \\t// the cluster. This helps improve scheduler's performance. Scheduler always tries to find\\n147: \\t// at least \\\"minFeasibleNodesToFind\\\" feasible nodes no matter what the value of this flag is.\\n148: \\t// Example: if the cluster size is 500 nodes and the value of this flag is 30,\\n149: \\t// then scheduler stops finding further feasible nodes once it finds 150 feasible ones.\\n150: \\t// When the value is 0, default percentage (5%--50% based on the size of the cluster) of the\\n151: \\t// nodes will be scored. It will override global PercentageOfNodesToScore. If it is empty,\\n152: \\t// global PercentageOfNodesToScore will be used.\\n153: \\tPercentageOfNodesToScore *int32 `json:\\\"percentageOfNodesToScore,omitempty\\\"`\\n154: \\n155: \\t// Plugins specify the set of plugins that should be enabled or disabled.\\n156: \\t// Enabled plugins are the ones that should be enabled in addition to the\\n157: \\t// default plugins. Disabled plugins are any of the default plugins that\\n158: \\t// should be disabled.\\n159: \\t// When no enabled or disabled plugin is specified for an extension point,\\n160: \\t// default plugins for that extension point will be used if there is any.\\n161: \\t// If a QueueSort plugin is specified, the same QueueSort Plugin and\\n162: \\t// PluginConfig must be specified for all profiles.\\n163: \\tPlugins *Plugins `json:\\\"plugins,omitempty\\\"`\\n164: \\n165: \\t// PluginConfig is an optional set of custom plugin arguments for each plugin.\\n166: \\t// Omitting config args for a plugin is equivalent to using the default config\\n167: \\t// for that plugin.\\n168: \\t// +listType=map\\n169: \\t// +listMapKey=name\\n170: \\tPluginConfig []PluginConfig `json:\\\"pluginConfig,omitempty\\\"`\\n171: }\\n172: \\n173: // Plugins include multiple extension points. When specified, the list of plugins for\\n174: // a particular extension point are the only ones enabled. If an extension point is\\n175: // omitted from the config, then the default set of plugins is used for that extension point.\\n176: // Enabled plugins are called in the order specified here, after default plugins. If they need to\\n177: // be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\\n178: type Plugins struct {\\n179: \\t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\\n180: \\tPreEnqueue PluginSet `json:\\\"preEnqueue,omitempty\\\"`\\n181: \\n182: \\t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\\n183: \\tQueueSort PluginSet `json:\\\"queueSort,omitempty\\\"`\\n184: \\n185: \\t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \\\"PreFilter\\\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\\n186: \\tPreFilter PluginSet `json:\\\"preFilter,omitempty\\\"`\\n187: \\n188: \\t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\\n189: \\tFilter PluginSet `json:\\\"filter,omitempty\\\"`\\n190: \\n191: \\t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\\n192: \\tPostFilter PluginSet `json:\\\"postFilter,omitempty\\\"`\\n193: \\n194: \\t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\\n195: \\tPreScore PluginSet `json:\\\"preScore,omitempty\\\"`\\n196: \\n197: \\t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\\n198: \\tScore PluginSet `json:\\\"score,omitempty\\\"`\\n199: \\n200: \\t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\\n201: \\t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\\n202: \\tReserve PluginSet `json:\\\"reserve,omitempty\\\"`\\n203: \\n204: \\t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\\n205: \\tPermit PluginSet `json:\\\"permit,omitempty\\\"`\\n206: \\n207: \\t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\\n208: \\tPreBind PluginSet `json:\\\"preBind,omitempty\\\"`\\n209: \\n210: \\t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \\\"Bind\\\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\\n211: \\t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\\n212: \\tBind PluginSet `json:\\\"bind,omitempty\\\"`\\n213: \\n214: \\t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\\n215: \\tPostBind PluginSet `json:\\\"postBind,omitempty\\\"`\\n216: \\n217: \\t// MultiPoint is a simplified config section to enable plugins for all valid extension points.\\n218: \\t// Plugins enabled through MultiPoint will automatically register for every individual extension\\n219: \\t// point the plugin has implemented. Disabling a plugin through MultiPoint disables that behavior.\\n220: \\t// The same is true for disabling \\\"*\\\" through MultiPoint (no default plugins will be automatically registered).\\n221: \\t// Plugins can still be disabled through their individual extension points.\\n222: \\t//\\n223: \\t// In terms of precedence, plugin config follows this basic hierarchy\\n224: \\t//   1. Specific extension points\\n225: \\t//   2. Explicitly configured MultiPoint plugins\\n226: \\t//   3. The set of default plugins, as MultiPoint plugins\\n227: \\t// This implies that a higher precedence plugin will run first and overwrite any settings within MultiPoint.\\n228: \\t// Explicitly user-configured plugins also take a higher precedence over default plugins.\\n229: \\t// Within this hierarchy, an Enabled setting takes precedence over Disabled. For example, if a plugin is\\n230: \\t// set in both `multiPoint.Enabled` and `multiPoint.Disabled`, the plugin will be enabled. Similarly,\\n231: \\t// including `multiPoint.Disabled = '*'` and `multiPoint.Enabled = pluginA` will still register that specific\\n232: \\t// plugin through MultiPoint. This follows the same behavior as all other extension point configurations.\\n233: \\tMultiPoint PluginSet `json:\\\"multiPoint,omitempty\\\"`\\n234: }\\n235: \\n236: // PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\\n237: // If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\\n238: type PluginSet struct {\\n239: \\t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\\n240: \\t// If the default plugin is also configured in the scheduler config file, the weight of plugin will\\n241: \\t// be overridden accordingly.\\n242: \\t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\\n243: \\t// +listType=atomic\\n244: \\tEnabled []Plugin `json:\\\"enabled,omitempty\\\"`\\n245: \\t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\\n246: \\t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \\\"*\\\" should be provided.\\n247: \\t// +listType=map\\n248: \\t// +listMapKey=name\\n249: \\tDisabled []Plugin `json:\\\"disabled,omitempty\\\"`\\n250: }\\n251: \\n252: // Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. Weight is used only for Score plugins.\\n253: type Plugin struct {\\n254: \\t// Name defines the name of plugin\\n255: \\tName string `json:\\\"name\\\"`\\n256: \\t// Weight defines the weight of plugin, only used for Score plugins.\\n257: \\tWeight *int32 `json:\\\"weight,omitempty\\\"`\\n258: }\\n259: \\n260: // PluginConfig specifies arguments that should be passed to a plugin at the time of initialization.\\n261: // A plugin that is invoked at multiple extension points is initialized once. Args can have arbitrary structure.\\n262: // It is up to the plugin to process these Args.\\n263: type PluginConfig struct {\\n264: \\t// Name defines the name of plugin being configured\\n265: \\tName string `json:\\\"name\\\"`\\n266: \\t// Args defines the arguments passed to the plugins at the time of initialization. Args can have arbitrary structure.\\n267: \\tArgs runtime.RawExtension `json:\\\"args,omitempty\\\"`\\n268: }\\n269: \\n270: func (c *PluginConfig) decodeNestedObjects(d runtime.Decoder) error {\\n271: \\tgvk := SchemeGroupVersion.WithKind(c.Name + \\\"Args\\\")\\n272: \\t// dry-run to detect and skip out-of-tree plugin args.\\n273: \\tif _, _, err := d.Decode(nil, &gvk, nil); runtime.IsNotRegisteredError(err) {\\n274: \\t\\treturn nil\\n275: \\t}\\n276: \\n277: \\tvar strictDecodingErr error\\n278: \\tobj, parsedGvk, err := d.Decode(c.Args.Raw, &gvk, nil)\\n279: \\tif err != nil {\\n280: \\t\\tdecodingArgsErr := fmt.Errorf(\\\"decoding args for plugin %s: %w\\\", c.Name, err)\\n281: \\t\\tif obj != nil && runtime.IsStrictDecodingError(err) {\\n282: \\t\\t\\tstrictDecodingErr = runtime.NewStrictDecodingError([]error{decodingArgsErr})\\n283: \\t\\t} else {\\n284: \\t\\t\\treturn decodingArgsErr\\n285: \\t\\t}\\n286: \\t}\\n287: \\tif parsedGvk.GroupKind() != gvk.GroupKind() {\\n288: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"args for plugin %s were not of type %s, got %s\\\", c.Name, gvk.GroupKind(), parsedGvk.GroupKind())\\n289: \\t}\\n290: \\tc.Args.Object = obj\\n291: \\treturn strictDecodingErr\\n292: }\\n293: \\n294: func (c *PluginConfig) encodeNestedObjects(e runtime.Encoder) error {\\n295: \\tif c.Args.Object == nil {\\n296: \\t\\treturn nil\\n297: \\t}\\n298: \\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\\n299: \\terr := e.Encode(c.Args.Object, &buf)\\n300: \\tif err != nil {\\n301: \\t\\treturn err\\n302: \\t}\\n303: \\t// The <e> encoder might be a YAML encoder, but the parent encoder expects\\n304: \\t// JSON output, so we convert YAML back to JSON.\\n305: \\t// This is a no-op if <e> produces JSON.\\n306: \\tjson, err := yaml.YAMLToJSON(buf.Bytes())\\n307: \\tif err != nil {\\n308: \\t\\treturn err\\n309: \\t}\\n310: \\tc.Args.Raw = json\\n311: \\treturn nil\\n312: }\\n313: \\n314: // Extender holds the parameters used to communicate with the extender. Only one extender\\n330: \\t// can implement this function.\\n331: \\tBindVerb string `json:\\\"bindVerb,omitempty\\\"`\\n332: \\t// EnableHTTPS specifies whether https should be used to communicate with the extender\\n333: \\tEnableHTTPS bool `json:\\\"enableHTTPS,omitempty\\\"`\\n334: \\t// TLSConfig specifies the transport layer security config\\n335: \\tTLSConfig *ExtenderTLSConfig `json:\\\"tlsConfig,omitempty\\\"`\\n336: \\t// HTTPTimeout specifies the timeout duration for a call to the extender.
